      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n39920-3" target="نَصَارَى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n39924"/></foreign> [applied to the <hi rend="ital">Christians</hi>] is a rel. n. from <foreign lang="ar">نَاصِرَةُ</foreign>, [or Nazareth,] a town of Syria, (S, M, K,) also called <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانَةُ</foreign>, (Lth, IDrd, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانُ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">نَصُورِيَةٌ</foreign>, (M, Sgh, K,) without teshdeed, accord. to Sgh, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">نُصْرِىٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نُصْرَى</foreign>, (as in a copy of the M,) or <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَوَةُ</foreign>: (TA:) so originally, and then applied to such as hold the religion of its inhabitants: (Msb:) this is the opinion of the lexicologists; but it is of weak authority, though admissible as there are other anomalous rel. ns.: (M:) or [so in K, but in the S, and] <foreign lang="ar">نَصَارَى</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرِىٌّ</foreign>, (Kh, M, Msb, K,) like as <foreign lang="ar">مَهَارَى</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">مَهْرِىٌّ</foreign>; (Msb, K;) or of <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانٌ</foreign> (Kh, S, M) and <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانَةٌ</foreign>, (S,) like as <foreign lang="ar">نَدَامَى</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نَدْمَانٌ</foreign> (Kh, S, M) and <foreign lang="ar">نَدْمَانَةٌ</foreign>; (S;) but more probably of <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانٌ</foreign>, because this word has been sometimes used, whereas we have not heard <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرِىٌّ</foreign> used: (M:) and it is implied in the copies of the K, that <foreign lang="ar">أَنْصَارٌ</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانِىٌّ</foreign>; but correctly, it is a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نَصْرَانٌ</foreign>, without <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, as is said in the TS, and the L, in both of which is mentioned the saying of the poet, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَمَّا رَأَيْتُ نَبَطًا أَنْصَارَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">When I saw Nabatheans, Christians</hi>], meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَصَارَى</foreign>. (TA.)    </entryFree>28:T7fd,<entryFree id="n39926" key="نَاصِرٌ" type="main">

(M.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَنْصَارُ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">The Assistants of the Prophet;</hi> (M, K;) of [the tribes of] El-Ows and El-Khazraj; (TA;) being an epithet applied to them especially, (M, K,) and used as a subst., as though it were the name of a tribe, wherefore the rel. n. <foreign lang="ar">أَنْصَارِىٌّ</foreign> [which is used as sing.] is formed from it.
